<p>Tokyo's easternmost territory, the island of <a href="/wiki/Minamitorishima" title="Minamitorishima">Minamitorishima</a> in <a href="/wiki/Ogasawara,_Tokyo" title="Ogasawara, Tokyo">Ogasawara village</a>, is in the tropical savanna climate zone (Köppen classification <i>Aw</i>). Tokyo's Izu and Ogasawara islands are affected by an average of 5.4 typhoons a year, compared to 3.1 in mainland Kantō.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Tokyo" title="Architecture of Tokyo">Architecture in Tokyo</a> has largely been shaped by Tokyo's history. Twice in recent history has the metropolis been left in ruins: first in the <a href="/wiki/1923_Great_Kant%C5%8D_earthquake" title="1923 Great Kantō earthquake">1923 Great Kantō earthquake</a> and later after <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Tokyo" title="Bombing of Tokyo">extensive firebombing in World War II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spatial_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-spatial-85">[85]</a></sup> Because of this, Tokyo's urban landscape consists mainly of modern and contemporary architecture, and older buildings are scarce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-spatial_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-spatial-85">[85]</a></sup> Tokyo features many internationally famous forms of modern <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Tokyo" title="Architecture of Tokyo">architecture</a> including <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_International_Forum" title="Tokyo International Forum">Tokyo International Forum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asahi_Beer_Hall" title="Asahi Beer Hall">Asahi Beer Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mode_Gakuen_Cocoon_Tower" title="Mode Gakuen Cocoon Tower">Mode Gakuen Cocoon Tower</a>, <a href="/wiki/NTT_Docomo_Yoyogi_Building" title="NTT Docomo Yoyogi Building">NTT Docomo Yoyogi Building</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rainbow_Bridge_(Tokyo)" title="Rainbow Bridge (Tokyo)">Rainbow Bridge</a>. Tokyo also features two distinctive towers: <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Tower" title="Tokyo Tower">Tokyo Tower</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Skytree" title="Tokyo Skytree">Tokyo Skytree</a>, the latter of which is the tallest tower in both Japan and the world, and the second tallest structure in the world after the Burj Khalifa in Dubai.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-skytree_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-skytree-13">[13]</a></sup> Mori Building Co started work on Tokyo's new tallest building which is set to be finished in March 2023. The project will cost 580 billion yen ($5.5 billion).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tokyo also contains <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Parks_and_gardens_in_Tokyo" title="Parks and gardens in Tokyo">numerous parks and gardens</a>. There are four national parks in Tokyo Prefecture, including the <a href="/wiki/Fuji-Hakone-Izu_National_Park" title="Fuji-Hakone-Izu National Park">Fuji-Hakone-Izu National Park</a>, which includes all of the Izu Islands.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1508px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree_(cropped).JPG" title="Panoramic view of Tokyo from Tokyo Skytree"><img alt="" data-file-height="1294" data-file-width="5999" decoding="async" height="324" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree_%28cropped%29.JPG/1500px-Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree_%28cropped%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree_%28cropped%29.JPG/2250px-Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree_%28cropped%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree_%28cropped%29.JPG/3000px-Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree_%28cropped%29.JPG 2x" width="1500"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tokyo_from_the_top_of_the_SkyTree_(cropped).JPG" title="File:Tokyo from the top of the SkyTree (cropped).JPG"> </a></div>Panoramic view of Tokyo from <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Skytree" title="Tokyo Skytree">Tokyo Skytree</a></div></div></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Tokyo has enacted a measure to cut greenhouse gases. Governor <a href="/wiki/Shintaro_Ishihara" title="Shintaro Ishihara">Shintaro Ishihara</a> created Japan's first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emissions_cap_system" title="Emissions cap system">emissions cap system</a>, aiming to reduce <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas_emissions" title="Greenhouse gas emissions">greenhouse gas emission</a> by a total of 25% by 2020 from the 2000 level.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Tokyo is an example of an <a href="/wiki/Urban_heat_island" title="Urban heat island">urban heat island</a>, and the phenomenon is especially serious in its special wards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barry_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-barry-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> According to the Tokyo Metropolitan Government,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> the annual mean temperature has increased by about 3 °C (5.4 °F) over the past 100 years. Tokyo has been cited as a "convincing example of the relationship between urban growth and climate".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2006, Tokyo enacted the "10 Year Project for Green Tokyo" to be realized by 2016. It set a goal of increasing roadside trees in Tokyo to 1 million (from 480,000), and adding 1,000 ha of green space 88 of which will be a new park named "Umi no Mori" (Sea Forest) which will be on a reclaimed island in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Bay" title="Tokyo Bay">Tokyo Bay</a> which used to be a landfill.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> From 2007 to 2010, 436 ha of the planned 1,000 ha of green space was created and 220,000 trees were planted bringing the total to 700,000. In 2014, road side trees in Tokyo have increased to 950,000, and a further 300 ha of green space has been added.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-top-width:0;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><caption style="border-top:1px #aaa solid;border-left:1px #aaa <p>As of October 2012, the official <a href="/wiki/Intercensal_estimate" title="Intercensal estimate">intercensal estimate</a> showed 13.506 million people in Tokyo with 9.214 million living within Tokyo's 23 wards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population2015_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-population2015-94">[94]</a></sup> During the daytime, the population swells by over 2.5 million as workers and students commute from adjacent areas. This effect is even more pronounced in the three central wards of <a href="/wiki/Chiyoda,_Tokyo" title="Chiyoda, Tokyo">Chiyoda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ch%C5%AB%C5%8D,_Tokyo" title="Chūō, Tokyo">Chūō</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Minato,_Tokyo" title="Minato, Tokyo">Minato</a>, whose collective population as of the 2005 National Census was 326,000 at night, but 2.4 million during the day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-population_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-population-95">[95]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1889, the <a href="/wiki/Home_Ministry" title="Home Ministry">Home Ministry</a> recorded 1,375,937 people in <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_City" title="Tokyo City">Tokyo City</a> and a total of 1,694,292 people in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tokyo_Prefecture" title="Tokyo Prefecture">Tokyo-fu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> In the same year, a total of 779 foreign nationals were recorded as residing in Tokyo. The most common nationality was English (209 residents), followed by American (182) and Chinese nationals (137).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup>
</p>

<p>Tokyo has the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_by_GDP" title="List of cities by GDP">largest metropolitan economy in the world</a>. According to a study conducted by <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tokyo_Area" title="Greater Tokyo Area">Greater Tokyo Area</a> (Tokyo–Yokohama, TYO) of 38 million people had a total GDP of $2 trillion in 2012 (at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>), which topped that list.
</p><p>Tokyo is a major international finance center;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> it houses the headquarters of several of the world's largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Investment_bank" title="Investment bank">investment banks</a> and insurance companies, and serves as a hub for Japan's transportation, publishing, <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a> and broadcasting industries. During the centralized growth of Japan's economy following <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, many large firms moved their headquarters from cities such as <a href="/wiki/Osaka" title="Osaka">Osaka</a> (the historical commercial capital) to Tokyo, in an attempt to take advantage of better access to the government. This trend has begun to slow due to ongoing population growth in Tokyo and the high cost of living there.
</p><p>Tokyo was rated by the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a> as the most expensive (highest <a href="/wiki/Cost-of-living_index" title="Cost-of-living index">cost-of-living</a>) city in the world for 14 years in a row ending in 2006, when it was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Oslo" title="Oslo">Oslo</a>, and later <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>
</p><p>Tokyo emerged as a leading international <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">financial center</a> (IFC) in the 1960s and has been described as one of the three "command centers" for the <a href="/wiki/World_economy" title="World economy">world economy</a>, along with New York City and London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> In the 2020 <a href="/wiki/Global_Financial_Centres_Index" title="Global Financial Centres Index">Global Financial Centers Index</a>, Tokyo was ranked as having the fourth most competitive financial center in the world (alongside cities such as <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_New_York_City#Finance" title="Economy of New York City">New York City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_London#Financial_services" title="Economy of London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shanghai" title="Shanghai">Shanghai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco#Economy" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shenzhen" title="Shenzhen">Shenzhen</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zurich" title="Zurich">Zurich</a> in the top 10), and second most competitive in Asia (after Shanghai).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GFCI2_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-GFCI2-12">[12]</a></sup> The Japanese financial market opened up slowly in 1984 and accelerated its internationalization with the "Japanese Big Bang" in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Despite the emergence of Singapore and Hong Kong as competing financial centers, the Tokyo IFC manages to keep a prominent position in Asia. The <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Stock_Exchange" title="Tokyo Stock Exchange">Tokyo Stock Exchange</a> is Japan's largest <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a>, and third largest in the world by <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a> and fourth largest by share turnover. In 1990 at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_asset_price_bubble" title="Japanese asset price bubble">Japanese asset price bubble</a>, it accounted for more than 60% of the world stock market value.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> Tokyo had 8,460 ha (20,900 acres) of agricultural land as of 2003,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> according to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Agriculture,_Forestry_and_Fisheries_(Japan)" title="Ministry of Agriculture, Forestry and Fisheries (Japan)">Ministry of Agriculture, Forestry and Fisheries</a>, placing it last among the nation's prefectures. The farmland is concentrated in Western Tokyo. Perishables such as vegetables, fruits, and flowers can be conveniently shipped to the markets in the eastern part of the prefecture. <i><a href="/wiki/Komatsuna" title="Komatsuna">Komatsuna</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Spinach" title="Spinach">spinach</a> are the most important vegetables; as of 2000, Tokyo supplied 32.5% of the <i>komatsuna</i> sold at its central produce market.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>With 36% of its area covered by forest, Tokyo has extensive growths of <a href="/wiki/Cryptomeria" title="Cryptomeria">cryptomeria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chamaecyparis_obtusa" title="Chamaecyparis obtusa">Japanese cypress</a>, especially in the mountainous western communities of Akiruno, Ōme, Okutama, Hachiōji, Hinode, and Hinohara. Decreases in the price of timber, increases in the cost of production, and advancing old age among the forestry population have resulted in a decline in Tokyo's output. In addition, pollen, especially from cryptomeria, is a major <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seasonal_allergies" title="Seasonal allergies">allergen</a> for the nearby population centers. Tokyo Bay was once a major source of fish. Most of Tokyo's fish production comes from the outer islands, such as Izu Ōshima and Hachijō-Jima. <a href="/wiki/Skipjack_tuna" title="Skipjack tuna">Skipjack tuna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nori" title="Nori">nori</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Carangidae" title="Carangidae">aji</a></i> are among the ocean products.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Tokyo" title="Tourism in Tokyo">Tourism in Tokyo</a> is also a contributor to the economy. In 2006, 4.81 million foreigners and 420 million Japanese visits to Tokyo were made; the economic value of these visits totaled 9.4 trillion yen according to the Tokyo Metropolitan Government. Many tourists visit the various downtowns, stores, and entertainment districts throughout the neighborhoods of the <a href="/wiki/Special_wards_of_Tokyo" title="Special wards of Tokyo">special wards of Tokyo</a>. Cultural offerings include both omnipresent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_pop_culture" title="Japanese pop culture">Japanese pop culture</a> and associated districts such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shibuya,_Tokyo" title="Shibuya, Tokyo">Shibuya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harajuku" title="Harajuku">Harajuku</a>, subcultural attractions such as <a href="/wiki/Studio_Ghibli" title="Studio Ghibli">Studio Ghibli</a> anime center, as well as museums like the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_National_Museum" title="Tokyo National Museum">Tokyo National Museum</a>, which houses 37% of the country's artwork <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Treasures_of_Japan" title="National Treasures of Japan">national treasures</a> (87/233).
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Toyosu_Market" title="Toyosu Market">Toyosu Market</a> in Tokyo is the largest wholesale fish and seafood market in the world since it opened on October 11, 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> It is also one of the largest wholesale food markets of any kind. It is located in the <a href="/wiki/Toyosu" title="Toyosu">Toyosu</a> area of <a href="/wiki/K%C5%8Dt%C5%8D" title="Kōtō">Kōtō</a> ward. The Toyosu Market holds strong to the traditions of its predecessor, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tsukiji_Fish_Market" title="Tsukiji Fish Market">Tsukiji Fish Market</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nihonbashi" title="Nihonbashi">Nihonbashi</a> fish market, and serves some 50,000 buyers and sellers every day. Retailers, whole-sellers, auctioneers, and public citizens alike frequent the market, creating a unique microcosm of organized chaos that still continues to fuel the city and its food supply after over four centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup>
</p>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:10000x6300_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="775" data-file-width="1248" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/10000x6300_01.jpg/220px-10000x6300_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/10000x6300_01.jpg/330px-10000x6300_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/10000x6300_01.jpg/440px-10000x6300_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:10000x6300_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Metro" title="Tokyo Metro">Tokyo Metro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toei_Subway" title="Toei Subway">Toei Subway</a> are two main subway operators in Tokyo.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Shuto_expressway_shibaura_jct_ii.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="708" data-file-width="1000" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Shuto_expressway_shibaura_jct_ii.jpg/220px-Shuto_expressway_shibaura_jct_ii.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Shuto_expressway_shibaura_jct_ii.jpg/330px-Shuto_expressway_shibaura_jct_ii.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Shuto_expressway_shibaura_jct_ii.jpg/440px-Shuto_expressway_shibaura_jct_ii.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Shuto_expressway_shibaura_jct_ii.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Hamazakibashi JCT in <a href="/wiki/Shuto_Expressway" title="Shuto Expressway">Shuto Expressway</a></div></div></div>
<p>Tokyo, which is the center of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Tokyo_Area" title="Greater Tokyo Area">Greater Tokyo Area</a>, is Japan's largest domestic and international hub for rail and ground transportation. However, its airspace has been under the US military's exclusive control after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Public transportation within Tokyo is dominated by an extensive network of "clean and efficient"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> trains and subways run by a variety of operators, with buses, monorails and trams playing a secondary feeder role. There are up to 62 electric train lines and more than 900 train stations in Tokyo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shibuya_Crossing" title="Shibuya Crossing">Shibuya Crossing</a> is the "world's busiest pedestrian crossing", with around 3,000 people crossing at a time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asahi_2016-04-22_111-0"><a href="#cite_note-asahi_2016-04-22-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn_2019-08-25_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn_2019-08-25-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p>As a result of World War II, Japanese planes are generally forbidden to fly over Tokyo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Therefore, Japan constructed airports outside Tokyo. <a href="/wiki/Narita_International_Airport" title="Narita International Airport">Narita International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chiba_Prefecture" title="Chiba Prefecture">Chiba Prefecture</a> is the major gateway for international travelers to Japan. Japan's flag carrier <a href="/wiki/Japan_Airlines" title="Japan Airlines">Japan Airlines</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/All_Nippon_Airways" title="All Nippon Airways">All Nippon Airways</a>, have a hub at this airport. <a href="/wiki/Haneda_Airport" title="Haneda Airport">Haneda Airport</a> on the reclaimed land at <a href="/wiki/%C5%8Cta,_Tokyo" title="Ōta, Tokyo">Ōta</a>, offers domestic and international flights. As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, some flight routes into Haneda are permitted through Tokyo airspace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup>
</p><p>Various islands governed by Tokyo have their own airports. <a href="/wiki/Hachij%C5%8D-jima" title="Hachijō-jima">Hachijō-jima</a> (<a href="/wiki/Hachijojima_Airport" title="Hachijojima Airport">Hachijojima Airport</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miyakejima" title="Miyakejima">Miyakejima</a> (<a href="/wiki/Miyakejima_Airport" title="Miyakejima Airport">Miyakejima Airport</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Izu_%C5%8Cshima" title="Izu Ōshima">Izu Ōshima</a> (<a href="/wiki/Oshima_Airport" title="Oshima Airport">Oshima Airport</a>) have services to Tokyo International and other airports.
</p><p>Rail is the primary mode of transportation in Tokyo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> which has the most extensive urban railway network in the world and an equally extensive network of surface lines. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JR_East" title="JR East">JR East</a> operates Tokyo's largest railway network, including the <a href="/wiki/Yamanote_Line" title="Yamanote Line">Yamanote Line</a> loop that circles the center of downtown Tokyo. It operates rail lines in the entire metropolitan area of Tokyo and in the rest of the northeastern part of <a href="/wiki/Honshu" title="Honshu">Honshu</a>. JR East is also responsible for <a href="/wiki/Shinkansen" title="Shinkansen">Shinkansen</a> high-speed rail lines.
</p><p>Two different organizations operate the subway network: the private <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Metro" title="Tokyo Metro">Tokyo Metro</a> and the governmental <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Metropolitan_Bureau_of_Transportation" title="Tokyo Metropolitan Bureau of Transportation">Tokyo Metropolitan Bureau of Transportation</a>. The Metropolitan Government and private carriers operate bus routes and one <a href="/wiki/Toden_Arakawa_Line" title="Toden Arakawa Line">tram route</a>. Local, regional, and national services are available, with major terminals at the giant railroad stations, including <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Station" title="Tokyo Station">Tokyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shinagawa_Station" title="Shinagawa Station">Shinagawa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shinjuku_Station" title="Shinjuku Station">Shinjuku</a>.
</p><p>Expressways link the capital to other points in the Greater Tokyo Area, the Kantō region, and the islands of <a href="/wiki/Kyushu" title="Kyushu">Kyushu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shikoku" title="Shikoku">Shikoku</a>. To build them quickly before the <a href="/wiki/1964_Summer_Olympics" title="1964 Summer Olympics">1964 Summer Olympics</a>, most were constructed above existing roads.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Other transportation includes taxis operating in the special wards and the cities and towns. Also, long-distance ferries serve the islands of Tokyo and carry passengers and cargo to domestic and foreign ports.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Tokyo" title="Education in Tokyo">Education in Tokyo</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Tokyo" title="List of universities in Tokyo">List of universities in Tokyo</a></div>
<p>Tokyo has many universities, junior colleges, and vocational schools. Many of Japan's most prestigious universities are in Tokyo, including <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tokyo" title="University of Tokyo">University of Tokyo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hitotsubashi_University" title="Hitotsubashi University">Hitotsubashi University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meiji_University" title="Meiji University">Meiji University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Institute_of_Technology" title="Tokyo Institute of Technology">Tokyo Institute of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waseda_University" title="Waseda University">Waseda University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_University_of_Science" title="Tokyo University of Science">Tokyo University of Science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sophia_University" title="Sophia University">Sophia University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Keio_University" title="Keio University">Keio University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Some of the biggest <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_universities_in_Japan" title="List of national universities in Japan">national universities</a> in Tokyo are:
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="div-col">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Hitotsubashi_University" title="Hitotsubashi University">Hitotsubashi University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Graduate_Institute_for_Policy_Studies" title="National Graduate Institute for Policy Studies">National Graduate Institute for Policy Studies</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ochanomizu_University" title="Ochanomizu University">Ochanomizu University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Gakugei_University" title="Tokyo Gakugei University">Tokyo Gakugei University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Institute_of_Technology" title="Tokyo Institute of Technology">Tokyo Institute of Technology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Medical_and_Dental_University" title="Tokyo Medical and Dental University">Tokyo Medical and Dental University</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tokyo_University_of_Agriculture_and_Technology" title="Tokyo University of Agriculture and Technology">Tokyo University of Agriculture and Technology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tokyo_University_of_Foreign_Studies" title="Tokyo University of Foreign Studies">Tokyo University of Foreign Studies</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tokyo_University_of_Marine_Science_and_Technology" title="Tokyo University of Marine Science and Technology">Tokyo University of Marine Science and Technology</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tokyo_University_of_the_Arts" title="Tokyo University of the Arts">Tokyo University of the Arts</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Electro-Communications" title="University of Electro-Communications">University of Electro-Communications</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Tokyo" title="University of Tokyo">University of Tokyo</a></li></ul>
</div>
<p>There is only one non-national <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public university</a>: <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Metropolitan_University" title="Tokyo Metropolitan University">Tokyo Metropolitan University</a>. There are also a few universities well known for classes conducted in English and for the teaching of the Japanese language, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Globis_University_Graduate_School_of_Management" title="Globis University Graduate School of Management">Globis University Graduate School of Management</a>, <a href="/wiki/International_Christian_University" title="International Christian University">International Christian University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sophia_University" title="Sophia University">Sophia University</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Waseda_University" title="Waseda University">Waseda University</a>
</p><p>Tokyo is also the headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_University" title="United Nations University">United Nations University</a>.
</p><p>Publicly run kindergartens, elementary schools (years 1 through 6), and junior high (lower secondary) schools (7 through 9) are operated by local wards or municipal offices. Public senior high (upper secondary) schools in Tokyo are run by the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Metropolitan_Government_Board_of_Education" title="Tokyo Metropolitan Government Board of Education">Tokyo Metropolitan Government Board of Education</a> and are called "Metropolitan High Schools". Tokyo also has many private schools from kindergarten through high school:
</p>
<table>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nihon-Kagaku-Miraikan,Koto-ward,Tokyo,Japan.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Nihon-Kagaku-Miraikan%2CKoto-ward%2CTokyo%2CJapan.JPG/220px-Nihon-Kagaku-Miraikan%2CKoto-ward%2CTokyo%2CJapan.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Nihon-Kagaku-Miraikan%2CKoto-ward%2CTokyo%2CJapan.JPG/330px-Nihon-Kagaku-Miraikan%2CKoto-ward%2CTokyo%2CJapan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Nihon-Kagaku-Miraikan%2CKoto-ward%2CTokyo%2CJapan.JPG/440px-Nihon-Kagaku-Miraikan%2CKoto-ward%2CTokyo%2CJapan.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nihon-Kagaku-Miraikan,Koto-ward,Tokyo,Japan.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Miraikan" title="Miraikan">National Museum of Emerging Science and Innovation</a>, also known as "Miraikan"</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Takeshita_Street_in_December_2018.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4032" data-file-width="3024" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Takeshita_Street_in_December_2018.jpg/170px-Takeshita_Street_in_December_2018.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Takeshita_Street_in_December_2018.jpg/255px-Takeshita_Street_in_December_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Takeshita_Street_in_December_2018.jpg/340px-Takeshita_Street_in_December_2018.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Takeshita_Street_in_December_2018.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Takeshita_Street" title="Takeshita Street">Takeshita Street</a> in <a href="/wiki/Harajuku" title="Harajuku">Harajuku</a></div></div></div>
<p>Tokyo has many museums. In <a href="/wiki/Ueno_Park" title="Ueno Park">Ueno Park</a>, there is the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_National_Museum" title="Tokyo National Museum">Tokyo National Museum</a>, the country's largest museum and specializing in traditional <a href="/wiki/Japanese_art" title="Japanese art">Japanese art</a>; the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_National_Museum_of_Western_Art" title="The National Museum of Western Art">National Museum of Western Art</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ueno_Zoo" title="Ueno Zoo">Ueno Zoo</a>. Other museums include the <a href="/wiki/Miraikan" title="Miraikan">National Museum of Emerging Science and Innovation</a> in <a href="/wiki/Odaiba" title="Odaiba">Odaiba</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Edo-Tokyo_Museum" title="Edo-Tokyo Museum">Edo-Tokyo Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sumida,_Tokyo" title="Sumida, Tokyo">Sumida</a>, across the <a href="/wiki/Sumida_River" title="Sumida River">Sumida River</a> from the center of Tokyo; the <a href="/wiki/Nezu_Museum" title="Nezu Museum">Nezu Museum</a> in <a href="/wiki/Aoyama,_Tokyo" title="Aoyama, Tokyo">Aoyama</a>; and the <a href="/wiki/National_Diet_Library" title="National Diet Library">National Diet Library</a>, National Archives, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Modern_Art,_Tokyo" title="National Museum of Modern Art, Tokyo">National Museum of Modern Art</a>, which are near the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Imperial_Palace" title="Tokyo Imperial Palace">Imperial Palace</a>.
</p><p>Tokyo has many theaters for performing arts. These include national and private theaters for traditional forms of Japanese drama. Noteworthy are the <a href="/wiki/National_Noh_Theatre" title="National Noh Theatre">National Noh Theatre</a> for <a href="/wiki/Noh" title="Noh">noh</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Kabuki-za" title="Kabuki-za">Kabuki-za</a> for <a href="/wiki/Kabuki" title="Kabuki">Kabuki</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> Symphony orchestras and other musical organizations perform modern and traditional music. The <a href="/wiki/New_National_Theatre_Tokyo" title="New National Theatre Tokyo">New National Theater Tokyo</a> in <a href="/wiki/Shibuya" title="Shibuya">Shibuya</a> is the national center for the performing arts, including opera, ballet, contemporary dance and drama.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-about-nntt_120-0"><a href="#cite_note-about-nntt-120">[120]</a></sup> Tokyo also hosts modern Japanese and international pop, and rock music at venues ranging in size from intimate clubs to internationally known areas such as the <a href="/wiki/Nippon_Budokan" title="Nippon Budokan">Nippon Budokan</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%E4%B8%89%E7%A4%BE%E7%A5%AD%E3%83%BC%E5%AE%9D%E8%94%B5%E9%96%80.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1780" data-file-width="2432" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/%E4%B8%89%E7%A4%BE%E7%A5%AD%E3%83%BC%E5%AE%9D%E8%94%B5%E9%96%80.JPG/220px-%E4%B8%89%E7%A4%BE%E7%A5%AD%E3%83%BC%E5%AE%9D%E8%94%B5%E9%96%80.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/%E4%B8%89%E7%A4%BE%E7%A5%AD%E3%83%BC%E5%AE%9D%E8%94%B5%E9%96%80.JPG/330px-%E4%B8%89%E7%A4%BE%E7%A5%AD%E3%83%BC%E5%AE%9D%E8%94%B5%E9%96%80.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/%E4%B8%89%E7%A4%BE%E7%A5%AD%E3%83%BC%E5%AE%9D%E8%94%B5%E9%96%80.JPG/440px-%E4%B8%89%E7%A4%BE%E7%A5%AD%E3%83%BC%E5%AE%9D%E8%94%B5%E9%96%80.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E4%B8%89%E7%A4%BE%E7%A5%AD%E3%83%BC%E5%AE%9D%E8%94%B5%E9%96%80.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Sanja_Matsuri" title="Sanja Matsuri">Sanja Festival</a> in <a href="/wiki/Asakusa" title="Asakusa">Asakusa</a></div></div></div>
<p>Many different <a href="/wiki/Festivals_in_Tokyo" title="Festivals in Tokyo">festivals occur throughout Tokyo</a>. Major events include the Sannō at <a href="/wiki/Hie_Shrine" title="Hie Shrine">Hie Shrine</a>, the Sanja at <a href="/wiki/Asakusa_Shrine" title="Asakusa Shrine">Asakusa Shrine</a>, and the biennial <a href="/wiki/Kanda_Matsuri" title="Kanda Matsuri">Kanda</a> Festivals. The last features a parade with elaborately decorated floats and thousands of people. Annually on the last Saturday of July, an enormous <a href="/wiki/Fireworks" title="Fireworks">fireworks</a> display over the <a href="/wiki/Sumida_River" title="Sumida River">Sumida River</a> attracts over a million viewers. Once <a href="/wiki/Cherry_blossom" title="Cherry blossom">cherry blossoms</a> bloom in spring, many residents gather in Ueno Park, <a href="/wiki/Inokashira_Park" title="Inokashira Park">Inokashira Park</a>, and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shinjuku_Gyoen" title="Shinjuku Gyoen">Shinjuku Gyoen</a> National Garden for picnics under the blossoms.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Harajuku" title="Harajuku">Harajuku</a>, a neighborhood in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shibuya,_Tokyo" title="Shibuya, Tokyo">Shibuya</a>, is known internationally for its youth style, fashion<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harajuku_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harajuku-121">[121]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Cosplay" title="Cosplay">cosplay</a>.
</p><p>Cuisine in Tokyo is internationally acclaimed. In November 2007, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michelin_guide" title="Michelin guide">Michelin</a> released their first guide for fine dining in Tokyo, awarding 191 stars in total, or about twice as many as Tokyo's nearest competitor, Paris. As of 2017, 227 restaurants in Tokyo have been awarded (92 in Paris). Twelve establishments were awarded the maximum of three stars (Paris has 10), 54 received two stars, and 161 earned one star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Tokyo" title="Sports in Tokyo">Sports in Tokyo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Tokyo" title="Football in Tokyo">Football in Tokyo</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:New_national_stadium_tokyo_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2967" data-file-width="5280" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/New_national_stadium_tokyo_1.jpg/220px-New_national_stadium_tokyo_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/New_national_stadium_tokyo_1.jpg/330px-New_national_stadium_tokyo_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/New_national_stadium_tokyo_1.jpg/440px-New_national_stadium_tokyo_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:New_national_stadium_tokyo_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Japan_National_Stadium" title="Japan National Stadium">Japan National Stadium</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ryogoku_Kokugikan_Tsuriyane_05212006.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1152" data-file-width="1555" decoding="async" height="163" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Ryogoku_Kokugikan_Tsuriyane_05212006.jpg/220px-Ryogoku_Kokugikan_Tsuriyane_05212006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Ryogoku_Kokugikan_Tsuriyane_05212006.jpg/330px-Ryogoku_Kokugikan_Tsuriyane_05212006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Ryogoku_Kokugikan_Tsuriyane_05212006.jpg/440px-Ryogoku_Kokugikan_Tsuriyane_05212006.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ryogoku_Kokugikan_Tsuriyane_05212006.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Ry%C5%8Dgoku_Kokugikan" title="Ryōgoku Kokugikan">Ryōgoku Kokugikan</a> sumo wrestling arena</div></div></div>
<p>Tokyo, with a diverse array of sports, is home to two professional baseball clubs, the <a href="/wiki/Yomiuri_Giants" title="Yomiuri Giants">Yomiuri Giants</a> who play at the <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Dome" title="Tokyo Dome">Tokyo Dome</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Yakult_Swallows" title="Tokyo Yakult Swallows">Tokyo Yakult Swallows</a> at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meiji-Jingu_Stadium" title="Meiji-Jingu Stadium">Meiji-Jingu Stadium</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Japan_Sumo_Association" title="Japan Sumo Association">Japan Sumo Association</a> is also headquartered in Tokyo at the <a href="/wiki/Ry%C5%8Dgoku_Kokugikan" title="Ryōgoku Kokugikan">Ryōgoku Kokugikan</a> sumo arena where three official <a href="/wiki/Sumo" title="Sumo">sumo</a> tournaments are held annually (in January, May, and September). <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> clubs in Tokyo include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F.C._Tokyo" title="F.C. Tokyo">F.C. Tokyo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Verdy" title="Tokyo Verdy">Tokyo Verdy 1969</a>, both of which play at <a href="/wiki/Ajinomoto_Stadium" title="Ajinomoto Stadium">Ajinomoto Stadium</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ch%C5%8Dfu,_Tokyo" title="Chōfu, Tokyo">Chōfu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/FC_Machida_Zelvia" title="FC Machida Zelvia">FC Machida Zelvia</a> at Nozuta Stadium in <a href="/wiki/Machida,_Tokyo" title="Machida, Tokyo">Machida</a>. Basketball clubs include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hitachi_SunRockers" title="Hitachi SunRockers">Hitachi SunRockers</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toyota_Alvark_Tokyo" title="Toyota Alvark Tokyo">Toyota Alvark Tokyo</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tokyo_Excellence" title="Tokyo Excellence">Tokyo Excellence</a>.
</p><p>Tokyo hosted the <a href="/wiki/1964_Summer_Olympics" title="1964 Summer Olympics">1964 Summer Olympics</a>, thus becoming the first Asian city to host the <a href="/wiki/Summer_Olympic_Games" title="Summer Olympic Games">Summer Games</a>. The National Stadium, also known as the <a href="/wiki/National_Stadium_(Tokyo,_1958)" title="National Stadium (Tokyo, 1958)">Olympic Stadium</a>, was host to a number of international sporting events. In 2016, it was to be replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Japan_National_Stadium" title="Japan National Stadium">New National Stadium</a>. With a number of world-class sports venues, Tokyo often hosts national and international sporting events such as basketball tournaments, women's volleyball tournaments, tennis tournaments, swim meets, marathons, rugby union and sevens rugby games, football, American football exhibition games, judo, and <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">karate</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Metropolitan_Gymnasium" title="Tokyo Metropolitan Gymnasium">Tokyo Metropolitan Gymnasium</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Sendagaya" title="Sendagaya">Sendagaya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shibuya" title="Shibuya">Shibuya</a>, is a large sports complex that includes swimming pools, training rooms, and a large indoor arena. According to <i>Around the Rings</i>, the gymnasium has played host to the October 2011 artistic gymnastics world championships, despite the International Gymnastics Federation's initial doubt in Tokyo's ability to host the championships following the March 11 tsunami.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Tokyo was also selected to host a number of games for the <a href="/wiki/2019_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2019 Rugby World Cup">2019 Rugby World Cup</a>, and to host the <a href="/wiki/2020_Summer_Olympics" title="2020 Summer Olympics">2020 Summer Olympics</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2020_Summer_Paralympics" title="2020 Summer Paralympics">Paralympics</a> which had to be rescheduled to the summer of 2021 due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Japan" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Japan">COVID-19 pandemic in Japan</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Akihabara_Night.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Akihabara_Night.jpg/220px-Akihabara_Night.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Akihabara_Night.jpg/330px-Akihabara_Night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Akihabara_Night.jpg/440px-Akihabara_Night.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Akihabara_Night.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Akihabara" title="Akihabara">Akihabara</a> is the most popular area for fans of anime, manga, and games.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fuji_TV_headquarters_and_Aqua_City_Odaiba_-_2006-05-03_edit.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1344" data-file-width="2013" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Fuji_TV_headquarters_and_Aqua_City_Odaiba_-_2006-05-03_edit.jpg/220px-Fuji_TV_headquarters_and_Aqua_City_Odaiba_-_2006-05-03_edit.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Fuji_TV_headquarters_and_Aqua_City_Odaiba_-_2006-05-03_edit.jpg/330px-Fuji_TV_headquarters_and_Aqua_City_Odaiba_-_2006-05-03_edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Fuji_TV_headquarters_and_Aqua_City_Odaiba_-_2006-05-03_edit.jpg/440px-Fuji_TV_headquarters_and_Aqua_City_Odaiba_-_2006-05-03_edit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fuji_TV_headquarters_and_Aqua_City_Odaiba_-_2006-05-03_edit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Fuji_Broadcasting_Center" title="Fuji Broadcasting Center">FCG Building</a>, home of <a href="/wiki/Fuji_TV" title="Fuji TV">Fuji TV</a> headquarters</div></div></div>
<p>As the largest population center in Japan and the site of the country's largest broadcasters and studios, Tokyo is frequently the setting for many <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Japan" title="Cinema of Japan">Japanese movies</a>, television shows, animated series (<a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Web_comics" title="Web comics">web comics</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Light_novels" title="Light novels">light novels</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_games" title="Video games">video games</a>, and comic books (<a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a>). In the <i><a href="/wiki/Kaiju" title="Kaiju">kaiju</a></i> (monster movie) genre, landmarks of Tokyo are usually destroyed by giant monsters such as <a href="/wiki/Godzilla" title="Godzilla">Godzilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gamera" title="Gamera">Gamera</a>.
</p><p>Some Hollywood directors have turned to Tokyo as a backdrop for movies set in Japan. Postwar examples include <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tokyo_Joe_(1949_film)" title="Tokyo Joe (1949 film)">Tokyo Joe</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/My_Geisha" title="My Geisha">My Geisha</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Tokyo_Story" title="Tokyo Story">Tokyo Story</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/You_Only_Live_Twice_(film)" title="You Only Live Twice (film)">You Only Live Twice</a></i>; recent examples include <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kill_Bill" title="Kill Bill">Kill Bill</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fast_and_the_Furious:_Tokyo_Drift" title="The Fast and the Furious: Tokyo Drift">The Fast and the Furious: Tokyo Drift</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Lost_in_Translation_(film)" title="Lost in Translation (film)">Lost in Translation</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Babel_(film)" title="Babel (film)">Babel</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Wolverine_(2013_film)" title="The Wolverine (2013 film)">The Wolverine</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Avengers:_Endgame" title="Avengers: Endgame">Avengers: Endgame</a></i>.
</p><p>Japanese author <a href="/wiki/Haruki_Murakami" title="Haruki Murakami">Haruki Murakami</a> has based some of his novels in Tokyo (including <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Wood_(novel)" title="Norwegian Wood (novel)"><i>Norwegian Wood</i></a>), and <a href="/wiki/David_Mitchell_(author)" title="David Mitchell (author)">David Mitchell</a>'s first two novels <i><a href="/wiki/Number9dream" title="Number9dream">number9dream</a></i> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghostwritten_(novel)" title="Ghostwritten (novel)"><i>Ghostwritten</i></a> featured the city. Contemporary British painter <a href="/wiki/Carl_Randall" title="Carl Randall">Carl Randall</a> spent 10 years living in Tokyo as an artist, creating a body of work depicting the city's crowded streets and public spaces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_World_Service_-_Carl_Randall_interview_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_World_Service_-_Carl_Randall_interview-124">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC_News_-_Carl_Randall_interview_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News_-_Carl_Randall_interview-125">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tokyo_Portraits_by_Carl_Randall_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tokyo_Portraits_by_Carl_Randall-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BP_Portrait_Award_2013_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-BP_Portrait_Award_2013-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Japan_Portraits_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-Japan_Portraits-128">[128]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Tokyo is the founding member of the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Network_of_Major_Cities_21" title="Asian Network of Major Cities 21">Asian Network of Major Cities 21</a> and is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Local_Authorities_for_International_Relations" title="Council of Local Authorities for International Relations">Council of Local Authorities for International Relations</a>. Tokyo was also a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/C40_Cities_Climate_Leadership_Group" title="C40 Cities Climate Leadership Group">C40 Cities Climate Leadership Group</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sister_cities_and_states">Sister cities and states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sister cities and states">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Japan" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Japan">List of twin towns and sister cities in Japan</a></div>
<p>As of 2022<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Tokyo has <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinning</a> or friendship agreements with the following twelve cities and states:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TMG_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-TMG-129">[129]</a></sup>
</p>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r998391716" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 10em;">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, United States (since February 1960)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beijing" title="Beijing">Beijing</a>, China (since March 1979)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, France (since July 1982)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-P1_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-P1-130">[130]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>, Australia (since May 1984)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, South Korea (since September 1988)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>, Indonesia (since October 1989)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo_(state)" title="São Paulo (state)">São Paulo State</a>, Brazil (since June 1990)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, Egypt (since October 1990)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Moscow" title="Moscow">Moscow</a>, Russia (since July 1991)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, Germany (since May 1994)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, Italy (since July 1996)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, United Kingdom (since October 2015)</li></ul>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Friendship_and_cooperation_agreements">Friendship and cooperation agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Friendship and cooperation agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_academic_and_scientific_research">International academic and scientific research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tokyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: International academic and scientific research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Research_and_development_in_Japan" title="Research and development in Japan">Research and development in Japan</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_space_program" title="Japanese space program">Japanese space program</a> are globally represented by several of Tokyo's medical and scientific facilities, including the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Tokyo" title="University of Tokyo">University of Tokyo</a> and other <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Tokyo" title="List of universities in Tokyo">universities in Tokyo</a>, which work in collaboration with many international institutions. Especially with the United States, including <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> and the many private spaceflight companies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Space_Economy_in_Figures_How_Space_Contributes_to_the_Global_Economy:_How_Space_Contributes_to_the_Global_Economy_2019_p._72_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Space_Economy_in_Figures_How_Space_Contributes_to_the_Global_Economy:_How_Space_Contributes_to_the_Global_Economy_2019_p._72-133">[133]</a></sup> Tokyo universities have working relationships with all of the <a href="/wiki/Ivy_League" title="Ivy League">Ivy League</a> institutions (including <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Washington_Post_2012_134-0"><a href="#cite_note-Washington_Post_2012-134">[134]</a></sup> along with other <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">research universities</a> and development <a href="/wiki/Laboratory" title="Laboratory">laboratories</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford</a>, <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">MIT</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">UC</a> campuses throughout California,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-News_Center_2019_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-News_Center_2019-135">[135]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UTokyo-Berkeley_2017_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-UTokyo-Berkeley_2017-136">[136]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/University_of_New_Mexico" title="University of New Mexico">UNM</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sandia_National_Laboratories" title="Sandia National Laboratories">Sandia National Laboratories</a> in <a href="/wiki/Albuquerque,_New_Mexico" title="Albuquerque, New Mexico">Albuquerque</a>, New Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QuantumRes_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-QuantumRes-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UNM_Rikkyo_138-0"><a href="#cite_note-UNM_Rikkyo-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-United_States._Department_of_Energy_1999_p._166-PA54_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-United_States._Department_of_Energy_1999_p._166-PA54-139">[139]</a></sup> Other partners worldwide include <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oxford_University" title="Oxford University">Oxford University</a> in the United Kingdom,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-University_of_Oxford_Japan_Office_2019_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Oxford_Japan_Office_2019-140">[140]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Singapore" title="National University of Singapore">National University of Singapore</a> in Singapore,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_University_of_Tokyo_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_University_of_Tokyo-141">[141]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">University of Toronto</a> in Canada,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-University_of_Toronto_-_Learning_Abroad_2018_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-University_of_Toronto_-_Learning_Abroad_2018-142">[142]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tsinghua_University" title="Tsinghua University">Tsinghua University</a> in China.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-清华大学新闻网_2018_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-清华大学新闻网_2018-143">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
